The Sixth Proof: Infinite Parts Cannot Be Enclosed
Proof against infinite parts in a finite body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the intuitive argument that a finite body cannot contain an infinite number of parts because the infinite cannot be bounded.

Core Idea
Infinite parts cannot be contained between finite boundaries.

This lesson presents a simple yet powerful proof from intuition. The author argues that every finite body has two ends and two sides. If it were composed of infinite parts, then the infinite would be enclosed between finite enclosers, which is intuitively impossible. This proof closes the set of demonstrations against actual infinitude of parts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before interpreting.
Notice the concise structure: premise, condition, conclusion.
2
Identify the two premises
The passage states: (1) a finite body has two ends and two sides, (2) if there were infinite parts between them, then the infinite would be enclosed.
These premises are straightforward.
3
Understand the intuition
The conclusion 'that is impossible by intuition' means that it is self-evident that the infinite cannot be bounded. Reflect on why this seems obvious.
This is a key point in classical kalam: the impossibility is known directly.
4
Connect to the broader context
The passage ends by stating this concludes the set of proofs. Consider how this argument fits with the previous ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : إن الجسم المتناهي في الحجم والمقـدار ، قد حصل له طرفان ، وأحاط به جانبان . فلو حصل فيها بين هذين الطرفين والجانبين أجزاء غير متناهية ، لصار غير المتناهي محصوراً بين حاصرين ، وذلك محال بالبديهة . فهذه جملة الدلائل المذكورة في بيان : أنه يمتنع كون الجسم مؤلفاً من أجزاء لا نهاية لها بالفعل .
The sixth proof: The body that is finite in size and magnitude has two ends and is surrounded by two sides. If there were infinite parts between these two ends and sides, then the infinite would be enclosed between two enclosers, and that is impossible by intuition. So this is the summary of the proofs mentioned in explaining that it is impossible for the body to be composed of actually infinite parts.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof (al-ḥujja al-sādisah) against infinite parts in a body. It is a simple argument: every finite body has boundaries (two ends, two sides). If it were composed of an infinite number of parts, then an infinite number of parts would be contained between two boundaries. That would mean the infinite is enclosed (maḥṣūr) between two enclosers (ḥāṣirīn), which is impossible (muḥāl) by direct intuition (bil-badīha). The author then states that this concludes the set of proofs (jimlat al-dalā’il) demonstrating the impossibility of a body being composed of actually infinite parts.

Key Terms

جانبان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that infinite parts could be arranged in a bounded space if they are infinitely small.
Correction: The argument relies on the intuitive impossibility of the infinite being enclosed, regardless of the size of parts. The point is that 'infinite' cannot be bounded by finites.

The Sixth Proof: Infinite Parts in a Finite Body
Al-Matalib al-Aliyah presents the sixth demonstration and its atomist conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of the sixth proof against infinite parts in a finite body and its conclusion that the body must be composed of indivisible atoms (al-jawhar al-fard).

Core Idea
Infinite parts cannot be enclosed; thus finite bodies must be made of finite parts.

This lesson introduces the sixth argument from the Mutakallimun’s arsenal. It uses a simple observation about finite bodies having ends to show that infinite parts are impossible. From this, the theologians conclude that bodies are composed of indivisible atoms. Let’s examine the logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Let the author's flow of reasoning sink in before analyzing.
The passage is concise; each sentence carries a logical step.
2
Identify the premise and conditional
The argument starts with a finite body having two ends and two sides. Then it poses a conditional: if infinite parts existed between them, the infinite would be enclosed.
3
Understand the impossibility
The conclusion that the infinite is enclosed between two enclosers is stated as intuitively impossible (bi-l-badīhah). Reflect on why this is self-evident.
4
Connect to the atomist conclusion
The author states that this completes the proofs that infinite parts are impossible, and that the mutakallimun derived from it the doctrine of the indivisible atom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : إن الجسم المتناهي في الحجم والمقدار ، قد حصل له طرفان ، وأحاط به جانبان . فلو حصل فيها بين هذين الطرفين والجانبين أجزاء غير متناهية ، لصار غير المتناهي محصوراً بين حاصرين ، وذلك محال بالبديهة . فهذه جملة الدلائل المذكورة في بيان : أنه يمتنع كون الجسم مؤلفاً من أجزاء لا نهاية لها بالفعل . أن المتكلمين كانوا يقولون : لما بطل هذا المذهب ، فقد ثبت القول بالجوهر الفرد .
The sixth argument: A finite body in size and magnitude has two ends and is surrounded by two sides. If between these two ends and the two sides there were infinite parts, then the infinite would become enclosed between two enclosers, and that is intuitively impossible. So this is the total of the proofs mentioned in demonstrating that it is impossible for a body to be composed of actually infinite parts. The mutakallimun (speculative theologians) used to say: Since this doctrine is invalid, the doctrine of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) is established.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth argument (al-ḥujjah al-sādisah) against the composition of a body from actually infinite parts. The argument begins with a finite body having two ends and two sides. If between these ends and sides there were infinite parts, then the infinite would be enclosed between two enclosers, which is impossible by intuition (bi-l-badīhah). The author concludes that this completes the proofs that it is impossible for a body to be composed of actually infinite parts. Then it notes that the mutakallimun derived from this the affirmation of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard), meaning that since infinite parts are impossible, there must be a smallest part – the atom.

Correction: The argument assumes a finite body from the start; it does not require further conditions.

The Philosophers' Objection and the Author's Rebuttal
Philosophers reject atomism; author argues proofs still refute infinite divisibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the philosophers' objection that disproving composition from infinite parts does not necessitate finite parts, by showing that the same proofs disprove the very premise of infinite divisibility.

Core Idea
Refuting infinite parts also refutes infinite divisibility.

The philosophers dismiss the previous arguments, claiming that the body is a simple entity not composed of parts, so the proofs against infinite parts are irrelevant to their doctrine. But the author turns the tables: since the philosophers believe in infinite divisibility, the same proofs that show the impossibility of infinite parts also disprove their premise. This passage is a classic example of dialectical refutation in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the philosophers' objection
Carefully read the first half of the passage where the philosophers state their objection: they reject atomism and claim the body is one simple thing, so disproving composition from infinite parts does not prove composition from finite parts.
Notice the dismissive tone: they accuse the author of ignorance.
2
Identify the author's rebuttal
Read the second half where the author responds: he reminds that they have already proven that infinite divisibility entails infinite parts, so the same proofs that refute actual infinite parts also refute the possibility of infinite divisibility.
The key move is that the philosophers' own premise (infinite divisibility) is refuted by the same arguments.
3
Understand the logical structure
Map the argument: (1) If a body is infinitely divisible, it must have infinite parts. (2) The author's previous proofs show that having infinite parts is impossible. (3) Therefore, the body cannot be infinitely divisible. So the philosophers' objection fails.
This shows the method of taking an opponent's premise and showing it leads to a contradiction.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The author ends with 'And God knows best', indicating humility before divine knowledge. Consider how this argument upholds atomism against the philosophers' view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفلاسفة : فقد استبعدوا هذا الكلام ، وحكموا على صاحبه بالجهل ، وقلة الفهم . وقالوا : إنه لا يلزم من إبطال تركب الجسم من أجزاء لا نهاية لها ، كونه مركباً من أجزاء متناهية. بل الحق : أن الجسم في نفسه شيء واحد ، ليس مركباً البتة من الأجزاء (۱) وحينئذ لا يبقى في ذكر هذه الدلائل منفعة في إبطال قولنا ومذهبنا . واعلم : أنا بينا بالوجوه القاطعة اليقينية : أن الجسم لو كان قابلاً لانقسامات لا نهاية لها ، لوجب كونه مركباً من أجزاء لا نهاية لها . فإذا ذكرنا هذه الدلائل في بيان أنه يمتنع كون الجسم مؤلفاً من أجزاء لا نهاية لها بالفعل . فحينئذ يلزم فساد المقدم ، وهو كونه قابلاً لانقسامات لا نهاية لها . وعلى هذا الطريق فإن هذه الدلائل ينتفع بها في إبطال قول الفلاسفة . والله أعلم .
As for the philosophers: they deemed this speech far-fetched, and judged its author to be ignorant and lacking understanding. They said: It does not follow from the refutation of the composition of the body from infinite parts that it is composed of finite parts. Rather, the truth is that the body in itself is one thing, not composed of parts at all. And then there remains no benefit in mentioning these proofs in refuting our statement and doctrine. Know: We have demonstrated with definitive certain proofs that if a body were receptive to infinite divisions, then it must be composed of infinite parts. So when we mention these proofs in demonstrating that it is impossible for a body to be composed of actually infinite parts, then the falsity of the premise follows, namely its being receptive to infinite divisions. And in this way, these proofs are beneficial in refuting the statement of the philosophers. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents the philosophers' objection and the author's rebuttal. The philosophers dismiss the above arguments as ignorance and lack of understanding. They claim that disproving composition from infinite parts does not necessitate composition from finite parts; rather, the body is one simple entity not composed of parts at all. Thus the proofs are useless against their view. The author responds by reminding that they have already demonstrated with certain proofs that if a body were infinitely divisible (qābil li-inqisāmāt lā nihāya lahā), it would be composed of infinite parts. Therefore, the same proofs that show the impossibility of actual infinite parts also show the falsity of the premise that the body is infinitely divisible. Hence these arguments do benefit in refuting the philosophers' position. The author concludes with 'Wallāhu aʿlam' (God knows best).

Key Terms
الفلاسفة
انقسامات لا نهاية لها
المقدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the philosophers' objection refutes atomism, making the author's arguments irrelevant.
Correction: The author argues that the philosophers' own premise (infinite divisibility) is refuted by the same arguments, so the objections are self-defeating.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

The Geometry of Asymptotes: Infinite Approach Without Meeting
Introduces the claim and presents Apollonius's proof of asymptotes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Apollonius's discovery of asymptotes demonstrates that indefinite approach does not necessitate meeting, supporting the broader theological doctrine.

Core Idea
Infinite approach does not imply eventual meeting.

This lesson delves into the first proof offered to support the claim that two magnitudes can perpetually approach each other without ever meeting. Apollonius, the ancient geometer, demonstrated this with asymptotes in his book Conics. Understanding this geometric fact is crucial for appreciating the logical foundations of certain theological positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim and proof
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a clear statement, then a proof introduced as 'the first of several aspects.'
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the central claim (two magnitudes approaching forever without meeting) and the source of the proof (Apollonius's Conics). Ask yourself what an asymptote is.
Asymptotes are lines that approach a curve but never touch it.
3
Reflect on the implication
Why does this geometric fact matter for theology? The author uses it to argue that infinite approach does not force meeting, countering a potential objection to the doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بهذا المذهب، لا يمتنع وجود مقدارين يتقاربان أبدأ ولا يلتقيان. والذي يدل على صحة ما ذكرناه: وجوه: الأول: إن أبلونيوس بين في كتاب المخروطات وجود خطين يتقاربان أبداً ولا يلتقيان. وذلك يدل على أن التزايد في القرب إلى غير النهاية لا يوجب حصول الالتقاء.
According to this doctrine, it is not impossible that two magnitudes exist that approach each other ever and do not meet. And that which indicates the correctness of what we mentioned: aspects: The first: Apollonius showed in the book of Conics the existence of two lines that approach each other forever and do not meet. And that indicates that the increase in proximity without end does not necessitate the occurrence of meeting.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a proof-by-authority. The author first states the claim: two magnitudes can approach each other indefinitely without meeting. Then he lists 'aspects' (wujūh) that support this. The first aspect is a citation from Apollonius's Conics, which demonstrates asymptotes—lines that approach a curve but never touch. The author argues that this geometrical fact proves that infinite approach does not entail convergence, thus supporting the initial claim.

Key Terms
خطين يتقاربان
التزايد في القرب
غير النهاية
الالتقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If two things get infinitely closer, they must eventually meet.
Correction: As Apollonius demonstrated with asymptotes, it is possible for two lines to approach each other indefinitely without ever meeting.

Checkpoint
What does the first proof rely on to demonstrate two lines that approach but never meet?
A) The Pythagorean theorem
B) The book of Conics by Apollonius
C) The definition of a square
D) The denial of the indivisible atom

Key Takeaway
Apollonius's asymptotes provide a concrete geometric counterexample to the idea that infinite approach forces meeting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your pursuit of closeness to Allah, have you ever felt discouraged because you haven't 'arrived' at a state you consider perfect? How would it change your heart to know that infinite approach without meeting is not only possible but is exactly what He desires?
?
What assumptions do you hold about your spiritual progress that, like the fallacy in this lesson, assume that drawing nearer must eventually lead to final attainment? Are you willing to let go of that expectation and persist in the approach regardless?
?
This lesson challenges a deep-seated assumption using geometry. What other assumptions about God, yourself, or others have you never examined? Will you dare to question them with the same honesty?

Second Proof: Infinite Bisection and Non-Meeting Lines
Geometric proof using infinite bisection to show approach without meeting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand a geometric argument that relies on the denial of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard) to prove that two lines can approach each other forever without meeting.

Core Idea
Infinite bisection shows that lines can approach forever without ever touching.

This lesson presents a geometric proof that builds on the denial of atomism. By imagining a square surface that can be divided infinitely, the author demonstrates that a dividing line can perpetually approach one side without ever reaching it. This argument reinforces the concept of infinite divisibility and the existence of asymptotic behavior.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the logical flow: premise, supposition, bisection, infinite repetition, conclusion.
The proof is short but dense; take your time.
2
Identify the key assumption
The proof begins by stating that geometry is built on denying the indivisible atom. Understand why this is necessary for the argument.
Without infinite divisibility, the bisection would stop.
3
Follow the bisection process
Imagine a square. Bisect it, then bisect the half, and so on. Notice that each new dividing line is closer to one side than the previous.
The lines are getting closer but never reach the side.
4
Grasp the contradiction
If the line ever reached the side, the square would be finitely divisible, contradicting the assumption of infinite divisibility.
This contradiction proves the conclusion.
5
Understand the conclusion
The proof establishes that two lines (the dividing line and the side) approach each other indefinitely without meeting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: إن علم الهندسة مبني على نفي الجوهر الفرد. إذا ثبت هذا، فلنفرض سطحاً مربعاً. بين أحد الضلعين والآخر بعد معين. فإذا نصفنا ذلك السطح، صار هذا الخط الذي أوجب التنصيف، أقرب إلى أحد الطرفين. فإذا نصفنا ذلك النصف، صار هذا الخط الثاني، أقرب. ثم لما كان ذلك السطح يقبل التنصيف إلى غير النهاية، فحينئذ يكون الخط القاسم، لا يزال يقرب من ذلك الطرف إلى غير النهاية. والبتة لا يصل إليه. إذ لو وصل إليه. لكان احتمال قبول ذلك السطح للقسمة متناهياً. وقد فرضناه غير متناه. فثبت: وجود خطين يتقاربان أبدا ولا يلتقيان.
Second: The science of geometry is built on the denial of the indivisible atom. If this is established, let us suppose a square surface. Between one side and the other there is a certain distance. When we bisect that surface, this line that caused the bisection becomes closer to one of the two ends. Then when we bisect that half, this second line becomes closer. Then since that surface accepts bisection without end, then the dividing line continuously approaches that end without end, and absolutely does not reach it. For if it were to reach it, the possibility of that surface accepting division would be finite, and we have supposed it infinite. So it is established: the existence of two lines that approach each other forever and do not meet.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a geometric proof that relies on the denial of atomism (jawhar fard). The author assumes a square surface that can be bisected infinitely. Each bisection produces a line closer to one side. Because the process can continue infinitely, the line keeps approaching but never reaches the side. If it did, the surface would be finitely divisible, contradicting the assumption of infinite divisibility. Therefore, two lines (the dividing line and the side) approach forever without meeting.

Key Terms
الجوهر الفرد
تنصيف
سطح مربع
غير متناه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a line gets closer and closer to a side through infinite divisions, it must eventually reach it.
Correction: The proof shows that because the division is infinite, the line never reaches the side; reaching would require a finite number of steps.

Checkpoint
What premise does the second proof rely on regarding geometry?
A) Geometry accepts the existence of the indivisible atom
B) Geometry is built on the denial of the indivisible atom
C) Geometry is based on the Pythagorean theorem
D) Geometry requires finite division

Key Takeaway
The proof shows that with infinite divisibility, two lines can approach each other forever without ever meeting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows two lines that approach each other forever but never meet. Think of your relationship with Allah. Are you truly approaching Him through your deeds, or are you content with the 'infinite distance' of never fully committing? What specific action will you take today to reduce that distance, knowing you may never fully 'reach' but must continue approaching?
?
The proof denies the indivisible atom—your soul is not a fixed point but infinitely divisible. Every moment you bisect your intention between this world and the next, always 'closer' but never fully there. Are you willing to accept that this infinite struggle is the very nature of faith? What one habit will you change to ensure your 'bisections' are consistently drawing you nearer to Allah, not just getting 'closer' without real progress?

Third Proof: Complementary Lines and Parallels
Uses two complementary lines to show infinite approach without meeting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the logical argument about complementary lines and parallels demonstrates infinite approach without meeting, and why meeting is impossible.

Core Idea
Two lines can approach each other infinitely without ever meeting.

This proof uses a geometric analogy to illustrate an important logical principle. It builds on a previous result about equality and shows that if two lines are arranged such that one approaches the other as a parallel recedes, they can get arbitrarily close but never converge. This reasoning will help you see how infinite regress works in a simple context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and the literal translation to get a sense of the flow and key terms.
Pay attention to the two lines: one parallel to width, one parallel to length.
2
Identify the two lines and their relationship
The proof introduces a width-parallel line and a length-parallel line. Notice how their positions are related: as the width-parallel moves farther, the length-parallel moves closer.
3
Understand the infinite regress
Since the width-parallel can be moved an infinite distance, the length-parallel's closeness also increases without bound. Grasp that this is an unending process.
This is the core of the argument.
4
Recognize the impossibility of meeting
If the length-parallel ever touched the length line, it would equal the whole surface, which is absurd. Hence, meeting is impossible despite infinite approach.
This refutes the misconception that infinite approach implies eventual meeting.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The proof establishes that the length-parallel forever approaches but never reaches or meets the length line.
This is a model for understanding infinite approximation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث: إنه ثبت في المقالة الأولى: أن المتهمين يجب كونهما متساويين. إذا عرفت هذا، فنقول: هذان المتممان، إنما يحدثان بسبب حصول خطين: أحدهما يوازي طول السطح، والثاني يوازي عرضه. ثم كلما كان الخط الموازي للعرض أبعد، عن الخط العرضي، صار الخط الموازي للطول، أقرب إلى الخط الطولي. ولما كان لا نهاية لمراتب بعد الخط الموازي للعرض، وجب أن يكون لا نهاية لمراتب قرب الخط الموازي للطول. والبتة لا يصل إليه. وإلا لصار ذلك الخط الطولي مساوياً لذلك السطح. وهو محال. فثبت: أن الخط الموازي للطول يقرب من الطول أبداً. والبتة لا يصل إليه. ولا يلقاه.
Third: It has been established in the first article that the two accused must be equal. If you know this, we say: These two complements arise only from the existence of two lines: one parallel to the length of the surface, and the second parallel to its width. Then whenever the line parallel to the width is farther from the width line, the line parallel to the length becomes closer to the length line. And since there is no end to the degrees of distance of the line parallel to the width, it is necessary that there be no end to the degrees of closeness of the line parallel to the length. And absolutely it does not reach it. Otherwise, that length line would become equal to that surface, which is impossible. So it is established: that the line parallel to the length approaches the length forever, and absolutely does not reach it, nor does it meet it.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a proof using parallelism. The author refers to a previous result about equality of 'the two accused' (likely a misprint for 'two complements'). He then considers a surface with two perpendicular directions: length and width. Two lines are drawn: one parallel to the width and one parallel to the length. As the width-parallel line moves farther from the width baseline, the length-parallel line moves closer to the length baseline. Since the width-parallel line can be moved an infinite distance, the length-parallel line approaches the length baseline an infinite amount but never reaches it, because reaching it would make the length line equal to the whole surface, which is impossible. Hence, the two lines (the length-parallel line and the length baseline) approach forever without meeting.

Key Terms
المتممان
موازي
الخط العرضي
الخط الطولي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Two lines that approach each other infinitely will eventually meet.
Correction: This proof shows that approach can be infinite without meeting; meeting would cause an absurdity (the length line would equal the whole surface).

Checkpoint

A) It moves farther away
B) It becomes closer to the length line
C) It intersects the length line
D) It remains stationary

Key Takeaway
The length-parallel line approaches the length line infinitely but never meets it, demonstrating an infinite approach without contact.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that the line approaches forever but never meets. Consider your spiritual journey: do you demand immediate perfection, or are you willing to take small steps of closeness, trusting that Allah values the direction of your heart even if you never arrive at a final state? What one action will you take today to move closer to your Lord, knowing the distance is infinite?
?
The proof shows that infinite closeness is possible without contact. This world is a realm of approach without full attainment. What is one worldly desire you chase thinking it will satisfy you fully, but which this proof shows can never be fully reached? How can you redirect that energy toward a relationship with Allah that rewards the journey itself?
?
If the length line did meet, it would become equal to the surface—an absurdity. In your life, what limits has Allah placed that you resent? Can you see them as signs of His wisdom and your finitude? This week, practice gratitude for one limitation that forces you to rely on Him.

Fourth Proof: Polygons and Infinite Approach
Geometric proof using polygons and external angles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the geometry of polygons demonstrates the possibility of two lines approaching each other indefinitely without meeting.

Core Idea
In polygons, increasing sides makes external angles approach zero but never reach it, showing asymptotic convergence.

This proof uses a concrete geometric example to illustrate that two lines can get arbitrarily close without meeting. By examining polygons with increasing numbers of sides, we see that the external angle shrinks but never vanishes, establishing the existence of asymptotically approaching lines.

Guided Path
1
Understand the geometric setup
Read the passage and picture a polygon with a side extended outward. Notice that this creates an external angle. This is the starting point of the proof.
Focus on the idea of extending a side of a polygon.
2
Follow the effect of increasing sides
As the number of sides increases, the internal angle widens, so the external angle narrows. This means the extended side gets closer to the line from the adjacent vertex.
The relationship is inverse: more sides → narrower external angle → closer approach.
3
Grasp the infinite and the impossible
Since there is no limit to the number of sides, the closeness can increase without bound. Yet it can never reach the adjacent line, because that would collapse the polygon into a straight line.
This proves two lines can approach forever without meeting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع: إن كل سطح مضلع، فإنه إذا أخرج ضلعه إلى الخارج حدثت زاوية في الخارج. وكلما كانت الأضلاع أكثر، كانت الزاوية الداخلة أوسع، فصارت الزاوية الحادثة في الخارج أضيق، فكان قرب ذلك الضلع من الخط الحادث في الخارج أزيد. ولما كان لا نهاية لمراتب المضلعات، فكذلك لا نهاية لمراتب ذلك القرب. مع أنه يستحيل أن يصل إليه، إذ لو وصل إليه، لاتصل أحد الضلعين بالضلع الآخر على الإستقامة. وحينئذ يصير الخط كله مستقيها، ويصير المضلع غير مضلع. فثبت وجود خطين يتقاربان أبداً ولا يلتقيان.
Fourth: For every polygonal surface, when its side is extended outward, an external angle occurs. And whenever the sides are more numerous, the internal angle becomes wider, so the external angle becomes narrower, and the closeness of that side to the line occurring outside increases. And since there is no end to the degrees of polygons, likewise there is no end to the degrees of that closeness. Yet it is impossible for it to reach it, because if it were to reach it, one of the two sides would connect to the other side in a straight line, and then the whole line would become straight, and the polygon would cease to be a polygon. So it is established: the existence of two lines that approach each other forever and do not meet.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a proof using polygon geometry. For any polygon, extending a side creates an external angle. As the number of sides increases, the internal angle widens, but the external angle narrows, meaning the extended side gets closer to the line from the adjacent vertex. Since polygons can have infinitely many sides, this closeness increases without bound, yet the extended side can never meet the adjacent side because if it did, the polygon would become a straight line, contradicting its definition. Thus, the two lines (the extended side and the line from the adjacent vertex) approach forever without meeting.

Key Terms
سطح مضلع
زاوية داخلة
زاوية خارجية
ضلع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that increasing sides eventually makes the polygon become a circle, where lines might meet.
Correction: The proof shows that even with infinite sides, the external angle never reaches zero, so the lines never meet. The polygon remains a polygon, not a circle.

Checkpoint
What happens to the external angle of a polygon as the number of sides increases?
A) It becomes wider
B) It becomes narrower
C) It remains constant
D) It disappears

Key Takeaway
Two lines can approach each other indefinitely without ever meeting, as shown by the geometry of polygons.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that increasing the sides brings the extended side closer to the adjacent line, but they never meet. In your relationship with Allah, you can increase your knowledge, worship, and closeness indefinitely. Yet you will never fully grasp His essence. Does this encourage you to keep striving or tempt you to become complacent? Write one concrete action you will take this week to draw closer to Allah, acknowledging that the journey has no end.
?
The polygon would cease to be a polygon if its sides met. What is one line in your life—a habit, thought, or association—that, if taken to its logical extreme, would undermine your identity as a Muslim? How can you adjust your path today to ensure you never cross that threshold?
?
This proof is a rational demonstration used to establish a truth about the physical world. How often do you use reason to examine your own beliefs? Take one belief you hold about God or the afterlife and test it with logical reasoning tonight. Where does it lead you?

Angles at Center and Polygons: A Geometric Proof of Asymptotic Approach
A geometric proof using polygons to demonstrate asymptotic approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fixed sum of angles at the center of a circle, combined with the geometric property of polygons, demonstrates that two lines can approach each other indefinitely without ever meeting.

Core Idea
Infinite approach is possible without meeting when the total angle is finite.

This lesson presents a geometric proof from the Imam using properties of circles and polygons. The argument shows that as the number of sides of an inscribed polygon increases, the sides of the triangles formed at the center approach each other arbitrarily closely, yet never meet because the total angle at the center is fixed at four right angles. This illustrates a key principle in kalam and mathematics: asymptotic approach without convergence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation to grasp the overall flow of the proof.
Pay attention to the key terms: 'زوايا عند المركز' (angles at the center), 'أربع قوائم' (four right angles), 'المعشر' (decagon).
2
Understand the geometric setup
The passage assumes a circle with a fixed total angle of 360° at its center. For any polygon inscribed in the circle, the number of triangles formed by drawing lines from the center to each side is two less than the number of sides.
For a decagon (10 sides), there are 8 triangles. Each triangle has its vertex at the center and its base as one side of the polygon.
3
Follow the logical progression
As the number of sides increases, so does the number of triangles. Since the total angle at the center remains constant, each triangle's vertex angle becomes narrower. Consequently, the two sides of each triangle (which are radii) become closer and closer, but because the total angle is finite, they never coincide.
This is the key insight: the sides approach each other indefinitely (asymptotically) but never meet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس: إن الزوايا الحادثة عند مركز الدائرة، لا تزيد على أربع قوائم البتة. ثم إنه ثبت أن كل مضلع يوجد، فإن عدد المثلثات الواقعة فيه، أقل عدد أضلاعه باثنين. فالمعشر يحصل فيه ثمانية مثلثات. فإذا أخرجنا من المركز خطين، إلى طرف الضلع الواحد من أضلاع المعشر، حدث منه مثلث واحد، رأسه عند المركز، وقاعدته ضلع ذلك المعشر. إذا ثبت هذا فنقول: كلما كانت الأضلاع أكثر، كانت المثلثات أكثر. وإذا كان لا نهاية لإمكان تزايد الأضلاع، فكذلك لا نهاية لحدوث المثلثات. وكلما كانت تلك المثلثات أكثر، كانت الزوايا أضيق، فكان أقرب أحد ذينك الضلعين من الآخر أكثر. فهذان الضلعان يتقاربان أبداً، ولا يلتقيان.
Fifth: The angles occurring at the center of a circle do not exceed four right angles at all. Then it has been established that for every polygon that exists, the number of triangles within it is two less than the number of its sides. So in a decagon (ten-sided polygon) there are eight triangles. When we draw from the center two lines to the endpoints of one side of the decagon, one triangle occurs, its vertex at the center and its base that side of the decagon. If this is established, we say: Whenever the sides are more numerous, the triangles are more numerous. And if there is no end to the possibility of increasing sides, likewise there is no end to the occurrence of triangles. And whenever those triangles are more numerous, the angles become narrower, so one of those two sides becomes closer to the other more. So these two sides approach each other forever and do not meet.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a proof using polygons inscribed in a circle. The total angle at the center is fixed at four right angles (360°). For a polygon, the number of triangles formed by drawing lines from the center to each side is two less than the number of sides. As the number of sides increases, the number of triangles increases, and the angle at the center for each triangle decreases (narrows). Consequently, the two sides of each triangle (which are radii) approach each other but never meet because the total angle is finite and the triangles fill it without division. Thus, the sides approach indefinitely without meeting.

Key Terms
زوايا عند المركز
أربع قوائم
مثلثات
المعشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If two lines continue to approach each other indefinitely, they must eventually meet.
Correction: The geometric proof shows that two lines can approach each other forever without meeting, as demonstrated by the radii of a circle when the number of triangles increases. The fixed total angle prevents them from ever coinciding.

Checkpoint
What is the total sum of angles at the center of a circle according to the passage?
A) Two right angles
B) Four right angles
C) Six right angles
D) Eight right angles

Key Takeaway
The geometric proof shows that two lines can approach each other indefinitely without ever meeting, because the total angle at the center is fixed and finite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that two lines can get infinitely close without ever meeting. In your spiritual life, is there a virtue, a relationship, or a sincere intention that you keep approaching but never fully commit to? What would it take to 'meet' that goal instead of just getting closer?
?
The total angle is fixed—every new triangle takes a share, but the sum never changes. Think about your time, energy, and focus. Are you dividing your finite resources into so many pursuits that each receives only a tiny sliver, preventing you from deeply achieving any? Is there one thing that deserves your full angle?
?
The radii never meet because of a logical necessity: the sum of angles is finite and each angle is positive. Are there truths in your faith that you accept as logically necessary, yet your actions treat them as optional? This proof demands consistency—what contradiction in your life needs to be resolved today?

Triangles and the Infinite Narrowing of Acute Angles
Classification of triangles by side numbers to show asymptotic lines.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the classification of triangles by angle type leads to the proof of the existence of lines that approach each other indefinitely without meeting.

Core Idea
Triangle side ratios reveal the asymptotic narrowing of acute angles.

This passage from Al-Matalib al-'Aliyah presents a geometric proof using Pythagorean triples and triangle classification. By examining sets of numbers representing side lengths, the author shows that only certain combinations yield triangles, and that the acute angle in an acute triangle can become infinitely narrow, implying the existence of asymptotes. Let's explore how this works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic then the translation. Notice the sequence of side-length sets.
2
Identify the four cases
The passage discusses four sets: (1,2,3) cannot form a triangle; (2,3,4) gives an obtuse triangle; (3,4,5) gives a right triangle; (4,5,6) gives an acute triangle. Understand why each falls into its category by comparing squares of sides.
Compare the square of the longest side to the sum of squares of the other two.
3
Understand the narrowing argument
The author claims that the acute angle in the acute triangle can be narrowed infinitely, making the two sides approach without meeting. This is the key conclusion.
Think about what happens as side lengths change—the acute angle becomes smaller indefinitely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس: إنا إذا أخذنا واحداً واثنين وثلاثة، وأردنا جعلهم واحداً، فقد تعذر. لأنه يلزم أن يكون مجموع ضلعين، مساوياً للضلع الثالث. وهو محال. وأما إن أخذنا الاثنين والثلاثة والأربعة، حصل منهم: مثلث منفرج الزاوية. لأن مربع الاثنين والثلاثة: ثلاثة عشر. ومربع الأربعة: ستة عشر. وأما إن أخذنا الثلاثة والأربعة والخمسة، حصل منهم: مثلث قائم الزاوية. لأن مربع الخمسة يساوي مجموع مربع الثلاثة، ومربع الأربعة. وأما إن أخذنا الأربعة والخمسة والستة حصل منهم: مثلثاً حاد الزوايا. لأن مربع وتر الزاوية العظمى، أقل من مجموع مربعي المحيطين بها. فقد ثبت: أن أول المثلثات حدوثاً: هو المثلث المنفرج الزاوية، ثم القائم الزاوية، ثم الحاد الزاوية. ثم إن مراتب هذه الزاوية الحادة في التضايق غير متناهية. فالضلعان المحيطان بها، كأنهما يتقاربان أبداً. ومن المحال التقاؤهما. فقد ثبت وجود خطين يتقاربان أبداً، ولا يلتقيان.
Sixth: When we take one, two, and three, and we want to make them one, it is impossible. Because it would require that the sum of two sides be equal to the third side, which is impossible. As for taking two, three, and four, we get from them an obtuse triangle. Because the square of two and three is thirteen, and the square of four is sixteen. As for taking three, four, and five, we get from them a right triangle. Because the square of five equals the sum of the square of three and the square of four. As for taking four, five, and six, we get from them an acute triangle. Because the square of the hypotenuse of the greatest angle is less than the sum of the squares of the two sides surrounding it. So it is established that the first of triangles in occurrence is the obtuse triangle, then the right triangle, then the acute triangle. Then the degrees of this acute angle in narrowness are infinite. So the two sides surrounding it, as it were, approach each other forever. And it is impossible for them to meet. So it is established: the existence of two lines that approach each other forever and do not meet.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a proof using the classification of triangles by angles based on side lengths. The author starts by showing that side lengths (1,2,3) cannot form a triangle because the sum of two smaller sides equals the third. Then he shows that (2,3,4) form an obtuse triangle (since sum of squares of smaller sides is less than square of longest), (3,4,5) form a right triangle (Pythagorean triple), and (4,5,6) form an acute triangle (sum of squares of smaller sides greater than square of longest). He concludes that the acute angle in the acute triangle can become infinitely narrow as the side ratio changes, meaning the two sides approach each other indefinitely but never meet. This demonstrates the existence of asymptotes.

Key Terms
مثلث منفرج الزاوية
مثلث قائم الزاوية
مثلث حاد الزاوية
وتر الزاوية العظمى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only right triangles are relevant for geometric proofs.
Correction: The proof uses the narrowing of acute angles to demonstrate asymptotes; right triangles are just one step in the classification.

Checkpoint
According to the sixth proof, which type of triangle is the first to occur?
A) Right triangle
B) Acute triangle
C) Obtuse triangle
D) Equilateral triangle

Key Takeaway
The infinite narrowing of acute angles demonstrates the existence of lines that approach but never meet.

The Fractional Example of Infinite Divisibility
Fractional example to show approach without meeting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fractional example demonstrates that infinite division leads to sums that never reach a larger unit, and how this applies to a line approaching but never reaching its end.

Core Idea
Infinite division means approach does not guarantee meeting.

The author begins with a mathematical example to illustrate a key consequence of infinite divisibility: a series of fractions can sum to something less than a simple fraction. This is then applied to a line dividing a unit, showing that the dividing line perpetually approaches the end without ever reaching it. This sets the stage for a larger argument against Euclidean geometry.

Guided Path
1
Read the fractional example
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the series of tenths. Notice that the sum of the series does not reach a ninth.
The series is: 1/10, 1/10^2, 1/10^3, ...
2
Understand the implication
Reflect on why the sum never reaches a ninth. This shows that with infinite division, you can get arbitrarily close but never equal a larger fraction.
3
Apply to the line
The author then applies this logic to a line dividing a unit. The dividing line keeps approaching the end but never reaches it, mirroring the fractional series.
This is the key transition from numbers to geometry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأجزاء المخوفة على تلك النسبة إلى غير النهاية ، إذا جمعت فليس تبلغ جملتها إلى الجزء ، الذي كان أعظم من الجزء الأول : مثاله : إن العشر ، وعشر العشر ، وعشر عشر العشر. وهكذا إلى أبعد الغايات ، وأبلغ النهايات . فإنه ليس يبلغ مجموعها إلى التسع . وكذلك : التسع ، وتسع التسع ، إلى أبلغ الغايات . لا يبلغ مجموعها إلى الثمن . وهكذا جميع الأجزاء . وأنت تعلم أن قسمة الواحد إلى الكسور ، لا يحتمله إلا الواحد المقداري . والخط القاسم له إلى تلك الأجزاء ، لا يزال يقرب من طرفه ، مع أنه لا يصل البتة إليه . فثبت بهذه الوجوه الأحد عشر : أن القائلين بقبول المقدار للقسمة إلى غير النهاية ، يلزمهم القول بوجود خطين يتقاربان أبداً ولا يلتقيان . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك ، فحينئذ لا تصح المصادرة التي ذكرها ( أقليدس ، لاحتمال أن يقال : هذان الخطان لا يتقاربان ، على ذلك الوجه الذي لا يلزم من تقاربهما تلاقيهما . وإذا كان هذا ممكناً ، لم يصح كلام ( أقليدس ) . واعلم : أن للشيخ مختصراً في علم الهندسة ، جمعها الكتاب و النجاة ، وذكر في إثبات هذه القضية : ( أن أحد الخطين لا بد وأن يميل إلى الآخر ، وإذا مال إليه لقيه لا محالة ، وهذا الكلام ضعيف . لأن قوله : و مال إليه : معناه : أنه يقرب منه . ونحن قد بينا بهذه الدلائل : أنه لا يلزم من تزايد القرب ، حصول الوصول . وأما ( الشيخ أبو علي بن الهيثم ، فقد حاول في كتاب « شرح المصادرات ، إقامة البرهان على صحة هذه القضية ، وطول فيه . وذكر في أثناء ذلك الدليل : مقدمة . وصححها بالكرة المتحركة . وهي مقدمة ضعيفة جداً . فثبت : أن على القول بكون المقدار، قابلاً للقسمة إلى غير النهاية ، توجب أن لا تصح هذه القضية [ أما إذا قلنا : إن قبول القسمة متناه . فحينئذ هذه القضية ] وليكن ههنا آخر كلامنا ، في تقرير دلائل القائلين بإثبات الجوهر الفرد وبالله التوفيق .
The fractions that are [؟] in that proportion ad infinitum, if gathered, their sum does not reach the part which is greater than the first part. Example: tenth, tenth of tenth, tenth of tenth of tenth, and so on to the farthest ends and most extreme limits – indeed their sum does not reach a ninth. Similarly: ninth, ninth of ninth, to the farthest limits – their sum does not reach an eighth. And so for all fractions. And you know that the division of the one into fractions is not borne except by the quantitative one. And the line dividing it into those fractions keeps approaching its end, yet it never reaches it at all. So it is established by these eleven ways that those who affirm the acceptance of magnitude for division ad infinitum are compelled to affirm the existence of two lines that perpetually approach each other but never meet. And if this is the case, then the postulate that Euclid mentioned is not valid, because it is possible to say: these two lines do not approach each other in such a way that their approaching necessitates their meeting. And if this is possible, Euclid's statement is not valid. And know that the Shaykh has a compendium on geometry, compiled in the Kitab and al-Najat, and he mentioned in proving this proposition that one of the two lines must necessarily incline to the other, and if it inclines to it, it meets it inevitably – this statement is weak. Because his saying 'inclined to it' means that it approaches it. And we have shown by these proofs that increasing closeness does not necessitate attainment. As for Shaykh Abu Ali ibn al-Haytham, he attempted in his book 'Sharh al-Musadarat' to establish a proof of the correctness of this proposition and prolonged it. And he mentioned in the course of that proof a premise and corrected it by the moving sphere – and that premise is very weak. So it is established that, on the view that magnitude is divisible ad infinitum, this proposition cannot be sound. [But if we say that the acceptance of division is finite, then this proposition holds.] And let this be the end of our speech in establishing the proofs of those who affirm the indivisible atom. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a complex argument that uses a mathematical example to refute the Euclidean postulate about converging lines and links this refutation to the debate on the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). The author begins by illustrating infinite divisibility with fractional parts: a tenth, a tenth of a tenth, and so on, never reaching a ninth. Similarly, a ninth series never reaches an eighth. This shows that dividing a unit into fractions requires a quantitative unit (al-wahid al-miqdari), and the line that divides it keeps approaching but never reaches the end. Through eleven unspecified ways (presumably previously given), it is established that those who accept infinite division must admit two lines that perpetually approach each other yet never meet. The author then argues that Euclid's postulate (likely the parallel postulate or something about lines meeting when they approach) becomes invalid, because it is possible that two lines approach without meeting. He then critiques two scholars: first, 'the Shaykh' (probably Ibn Sina) who in his works Kitab al-Shifa and al-Najat argued that one line must incline to the other and then meet—the author calls this weak, because 'incline' simply means 'approach', and we have shown that increasing proximity does not guarantee meeting. Second, Ibn al-Haytham attempted a proof in his commentary on Euclid's postulates, using a moving sphere, but that premise is also very weak. The conclusion: if magnitude is divisible infinitely, Euclid's proposition is unsound; if division is finite, the proposition holds. The author ends by stating that this concludes the proofs for the affirmers of the atom, invoking divine success.

Key Terms
قسمة إلى غير النهاية (division ad infinitum)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It equals 1/9.
B) It exceeds 1/9.
C) It does not reach 1/9.
D) It equals 1/8.

Key Takeaway
The fractional example shows that in a process of infinite division, the sum of all parts remains perpetually less than a larger unit, and a dividing line never reaches its endpoint.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever pursued a goal that seemed to get closer but never quite arrived—like mastering a skill or purifying a character trait? How does this truth about infinite approaches change how you view your own persistent efforts?
?
If God has set limits in creation (like the infinite approach without attainment), what does that tell you about your own need to trust His timing rather than demand completion now?
?
When you find yourself frustrated by slow progress in your faith journey (e.g., overcoming a sin), will you choose patience over despair, recognizing that the process itself may be the point—and that only Allah grants the final attainment?

Refuting Euclid and Defending the Indivisible Atom
Refutation of Euclid's postulate and critique of Ibn Sina and Ibn al-Haytham

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the failure of lines to meet despite infinite approach refutes Euclid's postulate and why the arguments of Ibn Sina and Ibn al-Haytham are insufficient.

Core Idea
If infinite division is allowed, Euclidean convergence fails.

Having established that infinite divisibility produces lines that perpetually approach without meeting, the author now strikes at a fundamental postulate of Euclid. He then defends this conclusion by critiquing two influential thinkers: Ibn Sina and Ibn al-Haytham. Their attempts to salvage the Euclidean proposition are shown to be weak, reinforcing the case for the indivisible atom.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the conclusion from eleven proofs
The author asserts that eleven ways have established that those who accept infinite division must admit two lines that approach eternally but never meet.
These eleven proofs are not detailed here; they are referenced from earlier discussion.
2
Understand the refutation of Euclid
If such lines exist, Euclid's postulate (likely about parallel lines or lines meeting when they approach) becomes invalid, because approach does not necessitate meeting.
3
Analyze the critique of Ibn Sina
Ibn Sina argued that one line must incline to the other and thus meet. The author calls this weak, equating 'incline' with 'approach', and notes that we have already shown approach does not guarantee meeting.
4
Analyze the critique of Ibn al-Haytham
Ibn al-Haytham attempted a proof using a moving sphere, but the author dismisses that premise as very weak.
5
Grasp the final conclusion
Thus, on the view of infinite divisibility, Euclid's proposition is unsound; only if division is finite does it hold. This concludes the proofs for the indivisible atom.

First Proof: Atoms Cannot Be Wholly Contiguous
First proof and first reason why atoms cannot be wholly contiguous.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the first proof argues that indivisible atoms cannot be wholly contiguous and how this leads to the impossibility of bodies composed of such atoms.

Core Idea
If atoms were wholly contiguous, composition would either increase volume or not — both impossible.

This passage presents the first of several proofs against atomic contiguity. It begins by stating the overall conclusion: indivisible atoms cannot be contiguous, so bodies cannot be formed from them. Then it focuses on the first part: why they cannot be wholly contiguous, using a dilemma about volume increase. Understanding this argument is key to the kalam critique of atomism.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the use of 'خلف' (contradiction) at the end.
2
Identify the main claim and dilemma
The passage claims that atoms cannot be wholly contiguous. The reason is a dilemma: if they were, either the volume increases or it does not. Identify these two cases.
This dilemma is the core of the proof.
3
Understand why both alternatives lead to contradiction
If volume increases, each atom is outside the other, so they are not wholly contiguous. If volume does not increase, then adding many atoms would never increase volume, contradicting observation. Both are impossible.
This shows that the assumption of whole contiguity is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي خمسة :
الفصل الأول
في
الدلائل المخرعة على المماسة
البرهان الأول : إن الأجزاء التي لا تتجزا ، يمتنع أن تكون متلاقية . وإذا كان كذلك ، امتنع حصول الأجسام عنها. إنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كونها متلاقية . لأنها لو تلاقت ، لكانت إما أن تكون متلاقية بالكلية ، أو لا بالكلية . والقسمان باطلان ، فوجب القول بأنه يمتنع كونها متلاقية
إنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كونها متلاقية بالكلية . لوجوه :
الأول : إنا إذا فرضنا جوهراً واحداً اتصل به جوهر ثاني فهل صار حجم مجموع الجزئين ، أزيد من حجم الجزء الواحد ، أو ما حصلت هذه الزيادة ؟ فإن كان الأول ، فحينئذ يكون كل واحد منها خارجاً عن ذات الآخر ، وغير نافذ فيه . وعلى هذا التقدير، فلم تصر كلية أحدهما ملاقية لكلية الآخر . وإن كان الثاني ، فحينئذ يكون مجموع الجزئين مساوياً في الحجم للجزء الواحد فحينئذ لو ضممنا إليه ثالثاً ورابعاً ، وجب أن لا تحصل الزيادة في الحجم. وحينئذ لا تكون هذه المقادير والأحجام ، متولدة عن تأليف هذه الأجزاء ، وقد فرضنا : أن الأمر كذلك . هذا خلف .
And they are five:
The first chapter
On
The proofs derived concerning contiguity.
The first proof: That indivisible parts cannot be mutually contiguous. If that is so, then bodies cannot arise from them. We say: They cannot be contiguous because if they were contiguous, they would either be wholly contiguous or not wholly contiguous. Both divisions are invalid, so it is necessary to say that they cannot be contiguous.
We say: They cannot be wholly contiguous. For reasons:
The first: If we suppose one atom (jawhar) to which a second atom attaches, then does the volume of the sum of the two parts become greater than the volume of the single part, or was this increase not produced? If the first, then each of them is outside the essence of the other and not penetrating into it. On this assumption, the whole of one is not contiguous with the whole of the other. If the second, then the sum of the two parts would be equal in volume to the single part. Then if we add a third and fourth to it, no increase in volume would occur. Then these magnitudes and volumes would not be generated from the composition of these parts, yet we have assumed that this is the case. This is a contradiction (khulf).
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage introduces the first proof of the chapter and presents its first reason. It begins by stating the overall proof: indivisible atoms cannot be contiguous, so bodies cannot be composed of them. Then it argues that they cannot be wholly contiguous by a dilemma: if two atoms join, either the volume increases or it does not. If it increases, each atom is outside the other, so they are not wholly contiguous. If it does not increase, then adding many atoms would never increase volume, contradicting the observable fact that compositions produce larger bodies. Both alternatives are impossible, proving that atoms cannot be wholly contiguous.

Key Terms
أجزاء لا تتجزأ (indivisible parts)
متلاقية (contiguous)
بالكلية (wholly)
حجم (volume)
خلف (contradiction)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that atoms could be partially overlapping, allowing contiguity without whole contiguity.
Correction: The proof only considers two possibilities: wholly contiguous or not wholly contiguous. It does not address partial overlap; the dilemma is about the definition of contiguity as complete contact. The proof shows that even if we assume whole contiguity, it leads to absurdity.

Checkpoint
According to the first reason, if two atoms join and the volume increases, what does that imply about contiguity?
A) They are wholly contiguous.
B) They are not wholly contiguous.
C) They interpenetrate.
D) They become one.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of atoms being wholly contiguous is demonstrated by a logical dilemma regarding volume increase, which leads to a contradiction in either case.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In the proof, the author presents a dilemma: either volume increases or it does not. Both lead to contradictions. Are you living with any belief that is similarly caught in a dilemma? What would it take for you to surrender that belief for the truth?
?
The proof shows that atoms cannot be wholly contiguous because it leads to absurdity. This means your physical body, which you rely on daily, is composed in a way that defies simple intuition. How does this humbling realization increase your awe of the Creator who designed such a world?
?
The author uses logical reasoning to reject a false assumption. When was the last time you allowed a sincere logical argument to change a deep-seated conviction? If you cannot recall, what does that say about your commitment to truth?

Interpenetration Leads to Oneness: The Second Reason
Second reason: If atoms interpenetrate, they lose distinction and become one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the impossibility of interpenetration follows from the identity of essences.

Core Idea
If atoms are identical in essence, they lose all distinction upon interpenetration.

This passage presents the second argument against atom interpenetration. The author shows that if atoms interpenetrate, they would become identical in all respects, eliminating multiplicity. Understanding this argument is crucial for grasping the rational proof that atoms must be distinct entities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Pay attention to the logical flow: if interpenetration, then no distinction, then oneness, which is impossible.
Notice the repeated emphasis on equality in essence, concomitants, and accidents.
2
Trace the conditional reasoning
Identify the main conditional claim and its justification. The author argues that interpenetration leads to no distinction because the parts are equal in essence. Follow how equality in essence leads to equality in properties.
The proof uses three levels: essence, concomitants, and accidents.
3
Understand the contradiction
The conclusion is that interpenetration would both remove multiplicity and yet multiplicity is assumed. Understand why this is a contradiction and why it proves interpenetration is impossible.
The argument does not rely on empirical evidence but on rational necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إن هذه الأجزاء إذا تداخلت ونفذ بعضها في بعض . فنقول : إنه لم يحصل الامتياز بينها في أمر من الأمور البتة . فوجب صيرورتها شيئاً واحداً . وذلك محال . إنما قلنا : إنه لم يحصل الامتياز في أمر من الأمور . لأن هذه الأجزاء متساوية في تمام الماهية. فتكون أيضاً : متساوية في لوازم الماهية . : فكل عارض يفرض عروضه لواحد منها ، فالآخر قابل له . لما بينا : أن تلك الأجزاء متساوية في تمام الماهية والمتساويات في تمام الماهية ، تكون متساوية في قبول العوارض . ووجود ذلك العارض بالنسبة إلى واحد منها ، و (۱) بالنسبة إلى الآخر . فيصير ذلك العارض أيضاً مشتركاً فيه
فثبت : أنه حصل الاشتراك بينها بأسرها في تمام الماهية ، وفي لوازم الماهية ، وفي عوارض الماهية . وحينئذ يرتفع الامتياز . وإذا زالى الامتياز ، فقـد بطل التعدد. فثبت : أن الأجزاء تماست بالكلية ، لما لم يتميز واحد منها عن الآخر . ويلزم ارتفاع التعدد وحصول التعدد . وكل ذلك محال .
The second [reason]: If these parts interpenetrate and some pass into others, we say: No distinction occurs between them in any matter whatsoever. So they must become one thing. That is impossible. We say: No distinction occurs in any matter because these parts are equal in the entirety of essence (mahiyya). So they are also equal in the concomitants (lawazim) of essence. So every accident (arad) that is supposed to attach to one of them, the other is receptive to it. Because we have shown that those parts are equal in the entirety of essence, and things equal in the entirety of essence are equal in receiving accidents. And the existence of that accident relative to one of them, and (1) relative to the other. So that accident also becomes shared.
Thus it is established that sharing occurs among all of them in the entirety of essence, in the concomitants of essence, and in the accidents of essence. Then distinction disappears. And when distinction vanishes, multiplicity ceases. So it is established that the parts become wholly contiguous, since one is not distinguished from the other. And it follows that multiplicity is removed and multiplicity occurs. All that is impossible.
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents the second reason why atoms cannot be wholly contiguous. It argues that if atoms interpenetrate, they would lose all distinction because they are identical in essence (mahiyya) and thus in all their properties (concomitants and accidents). Consequently, they would become one thing, but they were assumed to be many. This is a contradiction, proving that interpenetration is impossible.

Key Terms
تداخل (interpenetration)
امتياز (distinction)
ماهية (essence)
لوازم (concomitants)
عوارض (accidents)
تعدد (multiplicity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think interpenetration preserves distinguishability because atoms can remain distinct despite overlapping.
Correction: The argument shows that if atoms are identical in essence, they cannot be distinguished by any property upon interpenetration, so they become one.

Checkpoint
According to the second reason, why do interpenetrating atoms become one?
A) They are equal in volume.
B) They are equal in essence and accidents.
C) They are in different locations.
D) They repel each other.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of interpenetration is proven by the fact that identical essences lead to complete indistinguishability, contradicting multiplicity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

This lesson shows that if two things share an identical essence, they become entirely indistinguishable and thus one. Third Reason: Penetration Implies Division
Sanusi argues that interpenetration requires stages, implying divisibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the process of interpenetration would necessarily lead to the division of atoms, thus demonstrating its impossibility.

Core Idea
Interpenetration implies stages, and stages imply parts.

This passage presents the third rational argument against the possibility of complete interpenetration between two atoms. The argument is based on the observation that penetration must occur in distinct stages, each involving a different degree of contact. This forces the atom to have parts, contradicting its indivisible nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the three distinct stages described.
The passage uses terms like 'first', 'second', 'third' to mark stages.
2
Identify three stages of penetration
The passage describes: (1) tip contact, (2) during penetration, (3) complete penetration. Each stage has a different degree of contact.
These stages are crucial for the argument.
3
Understand why division is necessary
Different degrees of contact imply different 'amounts' of contiguity. This requires the atom to have parts that can be progressively contacted, leading to its division.
If atoms are indivisible, such stages cannot occur, hence interpenetration is impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالث في بيان أنه يمتنع حصول الملاقاة بالكلية : هو أن أحد المقدارين ، إذا نفذ في الثاني . فإنه يتصل طرف النافذ بطرف المنفوذ فيه أولاً ثم يأخذ في النفوذ ثانيا ، ثم في المرتبة الثالثة يحصل تمام النفوذ والمداخلة . ولا شك أن القدر الذي به حصلت الملاقاة بين النافذ وبين المنفوذ فيه ، عند اتصال طرف أحدهما بطرف الثاني ، أقل مرتبة من الملاقاة الحاصلة في أثناء النفوذ . والذي يحصل في أثناء النفوذ ، أقل قدراً مما يحصل عند تمام النفوذ . وذلك يوجب الانقسام للأجزاء . فثبت : أن بتقدير أن يصح القول بالمداخلة والنفوذ ، فإن القول بانقسام الأجزاء لازم
The third aspect in explaining that it is impossible for complete contiguity to occur: That when one of the two magnitudes penetrates into the second, the tip of the penetrating [part] first contacts the tip of the penetrated [part], then it proceeds in penetration secondly, then in the third stage complete penetration and interpenetration occurs. There is no doubt that the amount by which contiguity occurred between the penetrating and the penetrated, when the tip of one contacts the tip of the second, is a lesser degree than the contiguity occurring during penetration. And what occurs during penetration is lesser in amount than what occurs at complete penetration. That necessitates division of the parts. So it is established that if the thesis of interpenetration and penetration were valid, then the thesis of the division of parts would be necessary.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents the third reason. It argues that even if interpenetration were possible, the process would involve stages: first tip contact, then partial penetration, then full penetration. Each stage involves a different degree of contact, implying that the atoms have parts that come into contact progressively. Since atoms are defined as indivisible, this requirement for parts is a contradiction. Therefore, complete contiguity through interpenetration is impossible.

Key Terms
مقادير
نفوذ
طرف
مرتبة
انقسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Interpenetration is a single event that happens instantly without stages.
Correction: The reasoning shows interpenetration must involve a process with discrete stages, each with a different degree of contact, implying divisibility.

Checkpoint
The third reason shows that interpenetration implies what about atoms?
A) They are indivisible.
B) They are divisible.
C) They are immaterial.
D) They are eternal.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of stages in interpenetration forces atoms to have parts, contradicting their indivisibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi shows that even a hypothetical interpenetration would force an atom to have parts. If an atom cannot be penetrated without being divided, consider your heart: what worldly concerns have begun to 'penetrate' it? Is it still at the tip-contact stage, or has it progressed further? What concrete step will you take this week to preserve its indivisible devotion to Allah?

The Fourth Reason: Reductio ad Absurdum of Complete Interpenetration
Fourth reason: reductio ad absurdum of interpenetration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reductio ad absurdum argument that if complete interpenetration were possible, absurd consequences like a mountain fitting into a mustard seed would follow, thereby disproving interpenetration.

Core Idea
If atoms can interpenetrate completely, then a mountain could fit into a seed — an absurdity.

Ibn al-Murshid (Author) now presents the fourth argument against the possibility of complete contiguity (interpenetration) of atoms. This argument uses a reductio ad absurdum: assuming interpenetration leads to clearly impossible consequences. The passage uses vivid examples — a mountain and a mustard seed — to make the absurdity obvious. Let's examine the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Note the structure: a conditional (لو كان...) followed by a consequence (لوجب أن لا يمتنع...).
The argument is framed as 'If X were possible, then Y would be necessary'.
2
Understand the reductio reasoning
Identify the premise: complete interpenetration is possible. Then the absurd consequence: a great mountain could penetrate a single mustard seed, a great sea into a drop. Since these are impossible, the premise is false.
3
Reflect on the logical force
Consider why this is a strong argument. It shows that interpenetration has no limit; if possible at all, it would allow any size object to be compressed into any tiny space, which is empirically false.
4
Review the key terms
Familiarize yourself with the Arabic terms: جبل (mountain), خردلة (mustard seed), بحر (sea), قطرة (drop). These illustrate the extreme contrast in size.
The argument relies on the obvious impossibility of such compression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الرابع في بيان أنه يمتنع حصول الملاقاة بالكلية : إنه لو كان هذا ممكناً ، لوجب أن لا يمتنع نفوذ الجبل العظيم في الخردلة الواحدة ، وأن لا يمتنع نفوذ البحر العظيم في القطرة الواحدة. ولما كان كل ذلك محالاً ، كان القول بتداخل الأجزاء محالاً
And the fourth aspect in explaining that it is impossible for complete contiguity to occur: That if this were possible, then it would be necessary that the penetration of a great mountain into a single mustard seed would not be impossible, and that the penetration of a great sea into a single drop would not be impossible. And since all that is impossible, the thesis of interpenetration of parts is impossible.
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth reason, a reductio ad absurdum. If complete interpenetration were possible, there would be no limit to compression: a huge mountain could be compressed into a mustard seed, and a vast sea into a single drop. Since these are obviously impossible, the premise that atoms can interpenetrate is false.

Key Terms
جبل (mountain)
خردلة (mustard seed)
بحر (sea)
قطرة (drop)
تداخل (interpenetration)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Interpenetration might be possible only for small particles or in limited cases.
Correction: The argument shows that if complete interpenetration were possible at all, it would have no size limit, allowing any object to fit into any smaller space, which is absurd.

Checkpoint
The fourth reason shows that complete contiguity would lead to what absurdity?
A) Atoms would be infinite.
B) A mountain could fit into a mustard seed.
C) Atoms would be indivisible.
D) Bodies would be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The fourth reason uses a reductio ad absurdum: if complete interpenetration were possible, a mountain could fit into a mustard seed, which is impossible, so interpenetration is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your life have you been accepting a small inconsistency, not realizing that it logically leads to a larger absurdity? What would it take to root it out completely?
?
When you face an argument that seems reasonable at first, do you follow it to its logical conclusion to see if it leads to an impossible outcome? Identify a belief you hold that you have not tested this way.
?
The reductio reveals that a single false premise can force you into absurdity. Is there a premise in your own worldview that, if true, would make a mountain fit into a mustard seed? What would it take to abandon it?
